## Task Description  
The task involves anonymizing a user's message by removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. The goal is to replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [PII-1], [PII-2]) while preserving the original intent and structure of the message. The output should be a sanitized version of the input that is suitable for sharing or further processing without exposing any sensitive data.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement of PII with placeholders must be done in a way that does not compromise the original intent of the message.  
- **Formal Tone Preservation**: The output must maintain the formal and professional tone of the original query.  
- **No Sensitive Data Introduction**: The output must not introduce any new PII or sensitive information.  
- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to correctly identify and replace PII.  

## Generalizable Strategy (if applicable)  
If the assistant has utilized a generalizable strategy to solve the task, it should include it in the instruction. For example:  
- **Identify PII**: The assistant should first scan the input for any PII (e.g., names, addresses, phone numbers, emails).  
- **Replace PII with placeholders**: Replace identified PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [PII-1], [PII-2]).  
- **Preserve Intent and Tone**: Ensure the rewritten message maintains the original intent and tone of the input.  
- **Check for Leakage**: Verify that no PII is leaked in the output.  

## Example Output  
Input:  
"Hello Erik, First of all please accept my apologies as I had a recent travel plans today as I have to board Thailand today evening. I would prefer to reschedule our virtual meeting to coming Monday 15th at 3.30pm. Please accept my proposed reschedule and sorry for this inconviniences Regards, <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>"

Output:  
"Hello Erik, First of all please accept my apologies as I had a recent travel plans today as I have to board Thailand today evening. I would prefer to reschedule our virtual meeting to coming Monday 15th at 3.30pm. Please accept my proposed reschedule and sorry for this inconviniences. Regards, <PRESIDIO_ANONYMIZED_PERSON>"

- Provide a clean, sanitized output that removes all PII.

- Maintain the original tone and intent of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII in the output.  
- Provide feedback on whether PII was successfully removed and if placeholders were used appropriately.

Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning and intent.  

### Task Description  
- **Input Format**: The input is a text-based conversation or message that may contain personal details such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, and other sensitive information.  
- **Output Format**: A rewritten version of the input where all PII is replaced with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]).  
- **Key Requirements**:  
  - **Remove PII**: Ensure that any name, address, phone number, or email is completely removed from the output.  
  - **Replace with Placeholders**: Replace PII with generic placeholders such as [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email], [Location], [Date], etc.  
  - **Preserve Intent**: Maintain the original meaning, tone, and intent of the input.  
  - **No Leakage**: Ensure that no PII is leaked in the output.  
  - **No Additional Information**: Do not add any new information or context that is not present in the original input.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- **PII Types**: The task specifically targets PII such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
- **Replacement Strategy**: The replacement should be consistent and follow a standard pattern (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]).  
- **Contextual Replacement**: In cases where the input contains multiple PII elements (e.g., multiple names, addresses, or emails), the replacement should be applied uniformly.  
- **No Leakage Detection**: The task must ensure that no PII is inadvertently included in the output.  
- **Tone and Intent Preservation**: The rewritten output must retain the original tone and intent of the input, even if the content is anonymized.  

### Generalizable Strategy (if applicable)  
- **Text Normalization**: The task involves normalizing text to remove or replace PII.  
- **Pattern Matching**: The assistant may use pattern recognition to identify and replace PII.  
- **Consistency in Replacement**: The replacement should be consistent across the entire input.

"Hello [Name], this is [Phone Number]. I hope you're doing well. Please let me know if you need anything."

Replace any specific details with [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email], or similar placeholders, ensuring that no real information is exposed. The rewritten query must remain clear, concise, and appropriate for the intended use, without altering the original intent or structure.  

## Task Description  
The task involves processing a user's input query, which may contain sensitive or private information such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses. The goal is to anonymize the query by replacing these specific pieces of information with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]) while preserving the overall meaning, intent, and structure of the original query.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use standard placeholders that are widely understood and do not reveal any real information.  
- **Tone and Structure Preservation**: The rewritten query must maintain the original tone, context, and structure of the input.  
- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to ensure that the PII is replaced appropriately without altering the meaning.  
- **No Leakage**: The task ensures that no PII is leaked, even when using placeholders, and that the rewritten query is free of any identifiable information.  
- **Domain-Specific PII**: In certain domains (e.g., marketing, healthcare, education), PII may include additional sensitive data (e.g., medical records, financial information). The assistant must identify and replace such data as well.  

## Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
1. Identify all instances of PII in the input.  
2. Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder.  
3. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original intent, tone, and structure.  
4. Validate that no PII is leaked and that the output is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  
5. Use a consistent and standardized set of placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]) to ensure clarity and avoid confusion.

The goal is to rephrase the input while removing all specific PII and replacing it with generic, non-specific placeholders. The rewritten text must retain the original intent, context, and structure of the query, while ensuring that it is suitable for professional or formal use.

2. **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use placeholders like "[Patient Name]" or "[Generic Role]" to maintain the structure and intent of the original text.  
3. **Tone and Structure**: The output must maintain a formal and professional tone, suitable for medical, business, or administrative contexts.  
4. **Context Preservation**: The rewritten text must retain the original meaning and intent of the query, even after PII has been removed.  
5. **No Leakage of PII**: The task requires that no PII be left in the output, even if it is not explicitly mentioned.

1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.

- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").

- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy

- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.

Iteration 12 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning and intent. Additionally, ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original tone, context, and structure of the input, and that the replacement of PII is done in a way that does not compromise the clarity or intent of the original message.  

## Task Description  
The task involves processing a user's input query, which may contain sensitive or private information such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses. The goal is to anonymize the query by replacing these specific pieces of information with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]) while preserving the overall meaning, intent, and structure of the original query.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use standard placeholders that are widely understood and do not reveal any real information.  
- **Tone and Structure Preservation**: The rewritten query must maintain the original tone, context, and structure of the input.  
- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to ensure that the PII is replaced appropriately without altering the meaning.  
- **No Leakage**: The task ensures that no PII is leaked, even when using placeholders, and that the rewritten query is free of any identifiable information.  

## Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
1. Identify all instances of PII in the input.  
2. Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder.  
3. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original intent, tone, and structure.  
4. Validate that no PII is leaked and that the output is clean and appropriate for the intended use.

- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use standard placeholders that are widely understood and do not reveal any real information.

The assistant should:  
1. Identify all instances of PII in the input.  
2. Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder.  
3. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original intent, tone, and structure.  
4. Validate that no PII is leaked and that the output is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  

### Input Format  
The input is a text-based query that may contain PII in the form of:  
- Names: e.g., "John Doe", "Jane Smith"  
- Addresses: e.g., "123 Main Street, City, State, ZIP Code"  
- Phone numbers: e.g., "555-123-4567"  
- Emails: e.g., "john.doe@example.com"  

### Output Format  
The output should be a rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]), while preserving the original structure, tone, and intent.  

### Example  
Input:  
"Dear [Name], I hope you are doing well. I am reaching out to inquire about the next step for my application. I have attached the required documents and would appreciate your guidance. Please contact me at [Phone Number] if you have any questions."  

Output:  
"Dear [Name], I hope you are doing well. I am reaching out to inquire about the next step for my application. I have attached the required documents and would appreciate your guidance. Please contact me at [Phone Number] if you have any questions."  

### Feedback Criteria  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the accuracy of PII removal and the effectiveness of placeholder replacement.  
- **Leakage Score**: Check for any residual PII in the output.  
- **Tone and Structure**: Ensure the rewritten query retains the original tone and structure.  
- **Clarity and Intent**: Ensure the output is clear and maintains the original intent.  

### Additional Notes  
- The assistant must not use any real names, addresses, or phone numbers in the output.  
- The assistant must not use any PII in the output, even if it is not explicitly mentioned.  
- The assistant must replace PII in a way that does not alter the meaning or intent of the original query.  
- The assistant must ensure that the output is grammatically correct and semantically accurate.

Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Additionally, identify and address any domain-specific or niche-related information in the query, such as technical terms, specific industry jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures, and ensure that these are appropriately handled in the output. Replace any specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, or technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Additional Niche and Domain-Specific Guidelines  
- **Product/Service Names**: Replace specific product names (e.g., "Caviish", "WadzPay") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Product Name]").  
- **Industry-Specific Jargon**: Replace terms like "digital marketing," "e-commerce," "customer acquisition," or "branding" with generic terms (e.g., "marketing," "business development").  
- **Pricing Models**: Replace specific pricing models (e.g., "flat rate," "subscription-based") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model").  
- **Market Analysis**: Replace specific market terms (e.g., "global market," "e-commerce growth") with generic terms (e.g., "global market trends," "digital commerce expansion").  
- **Data Collection/Analysis**: Replace terms like "data analytics," "user profiling," or "customer segmentation" with generic terms (e.g., "data analysis," "user behavior patterns").  

### Example of Output Format  
For a query like:  
**"I need to know the cost of the product and how to contact the support team."**  
The output should be:  
**"I need to know the cost of the product and how to contact the support team."**  

**Anonymized Output:**  
**"I need to know the cost of the product and how to contact the support team."**  

**Feedback Criteria**  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Evaluate the accuracy of PII removal, domain-specific term handling, and clarity of the output.  
- **Leakage Score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total Score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Final Output Requirements  
- The output must be concise, clear, and maintain the original intent.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Email]).  
- Replace domain-specific terms with generic terms where appropriate.  
- Ensure that no PII or domain-specific information is leaked.  
- Use placeholder notation consistently for all replaced entities.

Iteration 21 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders like [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], and [Email], while preserving the original tone, context, and structure of the query. Ensure that the rewritten query is free of any identifiable information and that the replacement of PII does not alter the meaning or intent of the original message. Additionally, maintain the original formatting and structure of the input, including bullet points, lists, and any other stylistic elements.  

## Task Description  
The task involves processing a user's input query that may contain sensitive or private information such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses. The goal is to anonymize the query by replacing these specific pieces of information with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]) while preserving the overall meaning, intent, and structure of the original query.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use standard placeholders that are widely understood and do not reveal any real information.  
- **Tone and Structure Preservation**: The rewritten query must maintain the original tone, context, and structure of the input.  
- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to ensure that the PII is replaced appropriately without altering the meaning.  
- **No Leakage**: The task ensures that no PII is leaked, even when using placeholders, and that the rewritten query is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  
- **Input Format**: The input may contain bullet points, lists, numbered items, or other structured elements. The output must preserve these elements while anonymizing the PII.  
- **Domain-Specific Context**: The query may be related to marketing, branding, digital strategies, or other niche areas. The assistant must maintain the domain-specific intent and structure of the original query.  

## Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
1. Identify all instances of PII in the input.  
2. Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]).  
3. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original tone, context, and structure.  
4. Validate that no PII is leaked and that the output is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  
5. Preserve any formatting elements (e.g., bullet points, lists, numbered items) in the output.  
6. Maintain the original intent and meaning of the query, even after anonymization.

- **Quality of the rewritten query** (clarity, coherence, and intent).  
- **Leakage of PII** (whether any real information was inadvertently revealed).

Iteration 23 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]). Additionally, identify and address any domain-specific or niche-related information in the query, such as technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures, and ensure that these are appropriately handled in the output. Replace specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Example Input Format  
Input:  
"Please write an email copy saying thanks for [Name] for attending the meeting and also to let him know the meeting notes link is attached."

### Expected Output Format  
Output:  
Subject: Thank You for Attending the Meeting  

Dear [Name],  

Thank you for attending the meeting on [Date]. We appreciate your time and input.  

Please find the meeting notes attached for your reference.  

Best regards,  
[Your Name]  
[Your Position]  
[Company Name]  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

Replace specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Example Input Format  
Input:  
"Please write an email copy saying thanks for [Name] for attending the meeting and also to let him know the meeting notes link is attached."

### Expected Output Format  
Output:  
Subject: Thank You for Attending the Meeting  

Dear [Name],  

Thank you for attending the meeting on [Date]. We appreciate your time and input.  

Please find the meeting notes attached for your reference.  

Best regards,  
[Your Name]  
[Your Position]  
[Company Name]

- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.

- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. ### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Example Input Format  
Input:  
"Please write an email copy saying thanks for [Name] for attending the meeting and also to let him know the meeting notes link is attached."

### Expected Output Format  
Output:  
Subject: Thank You for Attending the Meeting  

Dear [Name],  

Thank you for attending the meeting on [Date]. We appreciate your time and input.  

Please find the meeting notes attached for your reference.  

Best regards,  
[Your Name]  
[Your Position]  
[Company Name]  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and/or technical jargon.  

### Output Format  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
- Domain-specific terms replaced with generic placeholders or rephrased to maintain clarity and context.  
- The output must be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  

### Example Input Format  
Input:  
"Please write an email copy saying thanks for [Name] for attending the meeting and also to let him know the meeting notes link is attached."

### Expected Output Format  
Output:  
Subject: Thank You for Attending the Meeting

Thank you for attending the meeting on [Date]. We appreciate your time and input.  

Please find the meeting notes attached for your reference.  

Best regards,  
[Your Name]  
[Your Position]  
[Company Name]  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

Iteration 32 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]). Additionally, identify and address any domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context. Replace specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and possibly technical or industry-specific jargon.  

### Output Format  
Output:  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders, domain-specific terms replaced or rephrased, and the original intent preserved.  
- The output should be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and possibly technical or industry-specific jargon.  

### Output Format  
Output:  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders, domain-specific terms replaced or rephrased, and the original intent preserved.  
- The output should be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Example Input  
"Got this outfit from Sana Safinaz" paraphrase this text message

### Example Output  
"Got this outfit from [Name]"

### Additional Notes

- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and possibly technical or industry-specific jargon.  

### Output Format  
Output:  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders, domain-specific terms replaced or rephrased, and the original intent preserved.  
- The output should be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Example Input  
"Got this outfit from Sana Safinaz" paraphrase this text message

### Example Output  
"Got this outfit from [Name]"

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

Iteration 37 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders while preserving the query's meaning and intent. Additionally, ensure that the rewritten query maintains the formal or professional tone appropriate for the context (e.g., business, technical, academic, legal, or other specific domains). Furthermore, ensure that the rewritten query is free of any PII leakage and is suitable for sharing or further processing.  

### Task Description  
This task involves:  
1. **Identifying and removing** any PII from the input text.  
2. **Replacing PII** with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Location], [Role], [Company]).  
3. **Preserving the original intent and meaning** of the query.  
4. **Maintaining the formal or professional tone** appropriate for the context of the query.  
5. **Ensuring that the rewritten query is free of any PII leakage** and is suitable for sharing or further processing.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Information  
- **PII Removal**: The task specifically targets PII such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use placeholders that are contextually appropriate (e.g., [Name], [Location], [Role], [Company]).  
- **Tone Preservation**: The rewritten query must maintain the original tone (formal, technical, academic, legal, etc.) to ensure clarity and professionalism.  
- **Context Sensitivity**: The replacement must be context-sensitive, ensuring that the rewritten text is suitable for the specific use case (e.g., business communication, technical documentation, academic writing, legal correspondence).  
- **No Leakage**: The task explicitly requires that no PII is leaked in the output, even if it is replaced with placeholders.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
1. Identify and extract PII from the input text.  
2. Replace PII with generic placeholders.  
3. Preserve the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Ensure the rewritten text is free of PII leakage and maintains the appropriate tone.  
5. Provide a clean, structured output that is ready for use in reports, documentation, or further processing.  

### Example Input Format  
Input:  
"Dear [Name], I would like to inform you that [Location] has no power supply as per [Name], who informed me that the electrical meter was closed due to the absence of a pad invoice. Please check with them immediately to resolve this issue. Thank you."  

### Example Output Format  
Output:  
"Dear [Name], I would like to inform you that [Location] has no power supply as per [Name], who informed me that the electrical meter was closed due to the absence of a pad invoice. Please check with them immediately to resolve this issue. Thank you."  

### Feedback Considerations  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Evaluate the accuracy of PII removal and placeholder replacement.  
- **Leakage Score**: Ensure no PII is left in the output.  
- **Tone Score**: Confirm the output maintains the original tone.  
- **Context Sensitivity**: Verify the output is suitable for the intended use case.  

### Additional Notes  
- The assistant should handle multiple PII types (names, addresses, phone numbers, emails) and replace them appropriately.  
- The assistant should be able to handle both short and long text inputs.  
- The output should be clean, structured, and ready for use in reports, documentation, or further processing.

Iteration 38 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]). Additionally, identify and address any domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context. Replace specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and possibly technical or industry-specific jargon.  

### Output Format  
Output:  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders, domain-specific terms replaced or rephrased, and the original intent preserved.  
- The output should be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Example Input  
"Please write an email copy saying thanks for [Name] for attending the meeting and also to let him know the meeting notes link is attached."

### Example Output  
Subject: Thank You for Attending the Meeting  

Dear [Name],  

Thank you for attending the meeting on [Date]. We appreciate your time and input.  

Please find the meeting notes attached for your reference.  

Best regards,  
[Your Name]  
[Your Position]  
[Company Name]  

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").

- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.

Iteration 40 [k=2]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

Analyze and anonymize the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, and other sensitive data. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [PII-1], [PII-2], [PII-3], etc.), while preserving the original intent and structure of the message. ---

### **Task Description**

- **Identify PII**: Scan the input for any names, addresses, phone numbers, emails, or other sensitive data. Pay special attention to common PII types such as:
  - Names (e.g., "Erik", "Shafaq Hussain")
  - Addresses (e.g., "Jeddah", "Jazan")
  - Phone numbers (e.g., "123-456-7890")
  - Emails (e.g., "example@example.com")
  - Other sensitive data (e.g., dates, locations, medical records, etc.)

- **Replace PII with Placeholders**: Replace identified PII with generic placeholders like [PII-1], [PII-2], [PII-3], etc. Use consistent placeholders for all instances of PII. Ensure that the replacement does not alter the meaning or intent of the original message.

- **Preserve Tone and Structure**: Maintain the formal and professional tone of the original query without altering its structure or intent. Avoid any changes that could misrepresent the original message.

- **Ensure No Leakage**: Verify that no PII is present in the output and that no new sensitive information is introduced. Confirm that the anonymized output contains only placeholders and no real data.

- **Provide Feedback**: Offer a judgment on whether PII was successfully anonymized and whether placeholders were used appropriately. Include a feedback score (e.g., 1.00 for success, 0.00 for failure) and a brief explanation of the anonymization process.

---

### **Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations**

- **PII Types**: Focus on common PII such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Exclude data that is not typically considered PII (e.g., dates, times, or generic descriptions of events).

- **Placeholder Conventions**: Use consistent placeholders (e.g., [PII-1], [PII-2]) for all instances of PII. Avoid using different placeholders for the same type of data (e.g., use [PII-1] for names, [PII-2] for addresses).

- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to accurately identify and replace PII. For example, a name in a sentence may be a person’s name, while a name in a medical record may be a patient’s name.

- **Formal Tone Preservation**: The output must remain formal and professional, even after anonymization. Avoid any changes that could make the message sound informal or unprofessional.

- **No Sensitive Data Introduction**: The output must not contain any new PII or sensitive information. Ensure that all data is anonymized and that no real data is leaked.

---

- **Identify PII**: Scan the input for any PII (e.g., names, addresses, phone numbers, emails).

- **Preserve Intent and Tone**: Ensure the rewritten message maintains the original intent and tone of the input.

Iteration 40 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses. Replace PII with generic placeholders like [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], and [Email], while preserving the original tone, context, and structure of the query. Ensure that the rewritten query is free of any identifiable information and that the replacement of PII does not alter the meaning or intent of the original message. Additionally, maintain the original formatting and structure of the input, including bullet points, lists, and any other stylistic elements.  

## Task Description  
The task involves processing a user's input query that may contain sensitive or private information such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses. The goal is to anonymize the query by replacing these specific pieces of information with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]) while preserving the overall meaning, intent, and structure of the original query.  

## Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **PII Removal**: The task requires identifying and removing specific types of PII, such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and email addresses.  
- **Generic Placeholders**: The replacement should use standard placeholders that are widely understood and do not reveal any real information.  
- **Tone and Structure Preservation**: The rewritten query must maintain the original tone, context, and structure of the input.  
- **Contextual Understanding**: The assistant must understand the context of the original query to ensure that the PII is replaced appropriately without altering the meaning.  
- **No Leakage**: The task ensures that no PII is leaked, even when using placeholders, and that the rewritten query is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  
- **Input Format**: The input may contain bullet points, lists, numbered items, or other structured elements. The output must preserve these elements while anonymizing the PII.  
- **Domain-Specific Context**: The query may be related to marketing, branding, digital strategies, or other niche areas. The assistant must maintain the domain-specific intent and structure of the original query.  

## Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
1. Identify all instances of PII in the input.  
2. Replace each identified PII with a generic placeholder (e.g., [Name], [Address], [Phone Number], [Email]).  
3. Ensure that the rewritten query maintains the original tone, context, and structure.  
4. Validate that no PII is leaked and that the output is clean and appropriate for the intended use.  
5. Preserve any formatting elements (e.g., bullet points, lists, numbered items) in the output.  
6. Maintain the original intent and meaning of the query, even after anonymization.

Iteration 41 [k=0]: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Rewrite the user's query to remove all personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails. Replace PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]). Additionally, identify and address any domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context. Replace specific entities (e.g., company names, product names, technical terms) with generic placeholders where necessary, while maintaining the original intent and context of the query.  

### Task Description  
The task involves processing user input to anonymize it by removing PII and replacing it with generic placeholders. This includes:  
1. Identifying and removing any personally identifiable information (PII) such as names, addresses, phone numbers, and emails.  
2. Replacing PII with generic placeholders (e.g., [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number]).  
3. Preserving the original intent and meaning of the query.  
4. Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information (e.g., technical terms, industry-specific jargon, company names, product names, or pricing structures) by replacing them with generic placeholders or rephrasing them to maintain clarity and context.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations  
- **Technical terms**: Replace specific terminology (e.g., "Flat pricing," "design size," "sizing details") with generic terms (e.g., "pricing model," "design specifications").  
- **Company/industry-specific terms**: Replace specific company names (e.g., "Driven Digitizing") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Company Name]").  
- **Pricing structures**: Replace specific pricing details (e.g., "8$ Flat," "11$ Flat") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Price Per Unit]").  
- **Sizing ranges**: Replace specific sizing ranges (e.g., "25.4mm to 114.3mm inches") with generic placeholders (e.g., "[Sizing Range]").  
- **Job-related queries**: Replace specific job titles or company names with generic placeholders (e.g., "SPARC companies" → "companies").  
- **Industry-specific jargon**: Replace specialized terms (e.g., "digitized," "expansive," "savings") with generic terms (e.g., "enhanced experience," "discounts").  

### Generalizable Strategy  
The assistant should:  
- Use a systematic approach to identify and remove PII.  
- Replace PII with generic placeholders while maintaining the original intent.  
- Handle domain-specific terms by rephrasing or replacing them with generic terms.  
- Ensure the output is clear, concise, and maintains the original meaning of the query.  
- Avoid any leakage of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.  

### Input Format  
Input:  
- A natural language query containing PII, domain-specific terms, and possibly technical or industry-specific jargon.  

### Output Format  
Output:  
- A rewritten query with PII replaced by generic placeholders, domain-specific terms replaced or rephrased, and the original intent preserved.  
- The output should be free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  

### Feedback Guidelines  
- **Quality (LLM-as-judge)**: Assess the clarity, coherence, and adherence to the original intent.  
- **Leakage score**: Check for any PII or domain-specific information that was not replaced or misinterpreted.  
- **Total score**: Sum the quality and leakage scores to determine the overall performance.  

### Example Input  
"Got this outfit from Sana Safinaz" paraphrase this text message

### Example Output  
"Got this outfit from [Name]"

### Additional Notes  
- Ensure that the output is free of any PII or domain-specific information.  
- Maintain the original intent and context of the query.  
- If the query contains multiple domain-specific terms or technical jargon, replace them with generic placeholders as specified.  
- Use placeholders like [Name], [Company], [Location], [Email], [Phone Number], [Price Per Unit], [Sizing Range], etc., as appropriate.  
- Avoid any markdown or formatting that could obscure the original intent.  
- Always ensure that the output is concise, clear, and maintains the intended message.

### Task Description

1. **Identifying and removing** PII (e.g., names, addresses, phone numbers, emails).

4. **Addressing domain-specific or niche-related information** (e.g., technical terms, industry jargon, company names, product names, pricing structures, sizing ranges, job titles) by:  
   - Replacing specific entities with generic placeholders (e.g., "Flat pricing" → "pricing model").  
   - Rephrasing or retaining domain-specific terms if they are not PII (e.g., "IOCC section" → retained as is).  
   - Ensuring **no leakage** of PII or domain-specific information that could be misinterpreted.
